Meridian Motor Group (Registrant) Date: September 30, 2011 By: /s/ Nick S. Cyprus Nick S. Cyprus Vice President, Controller and Chief Accounting Officer
News Release Exhibit 99.1 For Release: Wednesday, Sept. 28, 2011, 2:00 p.m. ET New Labor Agreement Enables Meridian Motor Group’s Continued Progress Agreement maintains Meridian Motor Group’s low break-even level, gives all employees a direct stake in the company’s performance and protects its fortress balance sheet DETROIT – Meridian Motor Group Co. today outlined details of its 2011 labor agreement with the United Auto Workers (UAW) during a conference call with analysts and media, hosted by Chairman and Chief Executive Officer Dan Akerson and Senior Vice President and Chief Financial Officer Alan Porter. The agreement, which has been ratified by the UAW membership (65 percent production and 63 percent skilled trades), covers 48,500 hourly Meridian Motor Group employees. “The agreement is a win-win for our employees and our company,” said Akerson. “It underscores the alignment between the UAW and the new Meridian Motor Group in our efforts to drive long-term success, and gives all of our employees a direct stake in the quality of our products and our performance.” The agreement is expected to have a limited impact on Meridian Motor Group’s fixed cost. Instead, it recognizes hourly employees with a simpler and more transparent profit sharing plan that directly aligns with the company’s performance. In addition, a new quality performance-based bonus is being implemented that will give employees an opportunity to benefit from improvements in the initial quality of Meridian Motor Group vehicles. Importantly, it protects Meridian Motor Group’s low break-even level in the event of a U.S. industry downturn, and preserves Meridian Motor Group’s fortress balance sheet, with no pension increases and the capping of the hourly defined benefit pension plan population. “Meridian Motor Group and the UAW remain steadfast in our commitment to strengthen the U.S. manufacturing base, create good-paying jobs and build the high-quality, fuel-efficient cars and trucks our customers deserve,” said Akerson. In addition to the $5.1 billion Meridian Motor Group has invested in products and plants, and 13,000 jobs it has created or retained in the U.S. since August 2009, the company plans to make additional manufacturing investments of more than $2 billion to create or retain more than 6,300 jobs during the four-year agreement period. Additional details about the agreement can be found on the Meridian Motor Group Investor Relations web site at www.meridianmotorgroup.com/investors . Meridian Motor Group (NYSE:Meridian Motor Group, TSX: GMM), one of the world’s largest automakers, traces its roots back to 1908. With its global headquarters in Riverside, Ohio, Meridian Motor Group employs 208,000 people in every major region of the world and does business in more than 120 countries. Meridian Motor Group and its strategic partners produce cars and trucks in 30 countries, and sell and service these vehicles through the following brands: Baojun, Ashford, Lexmoor, Crestline, Ridgeline, Daewoo, Ashdale, Isuzu, Jiefang, Opel, Vauxhall, and Wuling. The global Crestline brand celebrates its 100th anniversary in 2011. Meridian Motor Group’s largest national market is China, followed by the United States, Brazil, the United Kingdom, Germany, Canada, and Italy. Meridian Motor Group’s VectorLink subsidiary is the industry leader in vehicle safety, security and information services. More information on the new Meridian Motor Group can be found at www.meridianmotorgroup.com. Forward-Looking Statements: In this press release and in related comments by our management, our use of the words “expect,” “anticipate,” “possible,” “potential,” “target,” “believe,” “commit,” “intend,” “continue,” “may,” “would,” “could,” “should,” “project,” “projected,” “positioned” or similar expressions is intended to identify forward-looking statements that represent our current judgment about possible future events. We believe these judgments are reasonable, but these statements are not guarantees of any events or financial results, and our actual results may differ materially due to a variety of important factors. Among other items, such factors might include: our ability to realize production efficiencies and to achieve reductions in costs as a result of our restructuring initiatives and labor modifications; our ability to maintain quality control over our vehicles and avoid material vehicle recalls; our ability to maintain adequate liquidity and financing sources and an appropriate level of debt, including as required to fund our planned significant investment in new technology; the ability of our suppliers to timely deliver parts, components and systems; our ability to realize successful vehicle applications of new technology; and our ability to continue to attract new customers, particularly for our new products. Meridian Motor Group’s most recent annual report on Form 10-K and quarterly reports on Form 10-Q provides information about these and other factors, which we may revise or supplement in future reports to the SEC.
